<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Hideo Kojima</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">

<p><b>Hideo Kojima</b> <span style="font-weight: normal">(<span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja" xml:lang="ja">小島 秀夫</span><span class="t_nihongo_comma" style="display:none">,</span> <i>Kojima Hideo</i><sup class="t_nihongo_help noprint"><a href="/wiki/Help:Installing_Japanese_character_sets" title="Help:Installing Japanese character sets"><span class="t_nihongo_icon" style="color: #00e; font: bold 80% sans-serif; text-decoration: none; padding: 0 .1em;">?</span></a></sup>, born August 24, 1963)</span> is a Japanese <a href="/wiki/Video_game_design" title="Video game design">video game designer</a>, screenwriter, director, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Game_producer" title="Game producer">producer</a> who is regarded for his <a href="/wiki/Auteur" title="Auteur">auteur</a> approach to video games.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> He is the director of <a href="/wiki/Kojima_Productions" title="Kojima Productions">Kojima Productions</a>, which he founded in 2005,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-konami_pr_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-konami_pr-3">[3]</a></sup> and a former vice president of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Konami_Digital_Entertainment" title="Konami Digital Entertainment">Konami Digital Entertainment</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-promo_2011_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-promo_2011-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ign_bio_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-ign_bio-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>Kojima is the creator, director and writer of a number of <a href="/wiki/Video_game" title="Video game">video games</a>, including the <i><a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear" title="Metal Gear">Metal Gear</a></i> series of <a href="/wiki/Stealth_game" title="Stealth game">stealth games</a>, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Adventure_game" title="Adventure game">adventure games</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Snatcher_(video_game)" title="Snatcher (video game)">Snatcher</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Policenauts" title="Policenauts">Policenauts</a></i>. He also directed or produced games in other series, including <i><a href="/wiki/Zone_of_the_Enders" title="Zone of the Enders">Zone of the Enders</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Boktai" title="Boktai">Boktai</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Castlevania:_Lords_of_Shadow" title="Castlevania: Lords of Shadow">Castlevania: Lords of Shadow</a></i>.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Biography">Biography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hideo_Kojima&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Biography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hideo_Kojima&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Kojima was born in <a href="/wiki/Tokyo" title="Tokyo">Tokyo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ign_bio_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-ign_bio-5">[5]</a></sup> and moved to western Japan at the age of three. He said that early on in his life he already had to deal with death,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-edge136_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-edge136-6">[6]</a></sup> with his father passing away when he was only 13.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Parkin_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Parkin-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>When he was young, the Kojima family moved to a small city called Shirasaki.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-edge136_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-edge136-6">[6]</a></sup> Just as quickly, his family soon moved to <a href="/wiki/Kawanishi,_Hy%C5%8Dgo" title="Kawanishi, Hyōgo">Kawanishi, Hyōgo</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-businessweek_may09_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-businessweek_may09-8">[8]</a></sup> in the Kansai region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-edge136_6-2"><a href="#cite_note-edge136-6">[6]</a></sup> Kojima has noted that growing up he was a <a href="/wiki/Latchkey_kid" title="Latchkey kid">latchkey kid</a>, often having to look after himself when he came home from school.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-edge136_6-3"><a href="#cite_note-edge136-6">[6]</a></sup> Staying at home by himself in isolation still affects him to this day stating, "[whenever] I travel and stay at a hotel I put the TV on as soon as I enter the room, just to deal with the feeling of loneliness."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-edge136_6-4"><a href="#cite_note-edge136-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>He wanted to be an artist or illustrator, but he was often discouraged by societal norms of Japan which favored finding safe, well-paying jobs. He was also discouraged because his uncle was also an artist but suffered from financial difficulties. Another reason was his father's death which left his family more financially tight.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-edge136_6-5"><a href="#cite_note-edge136-6">[6]</a></sup> He eventually started writing short stories and began to send them to Japanese magazines but was never able to get anything published. He cites that his stories were often 400 pages long while most magazines wanted their short stories to be around 100 pages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-edge136_6-6"><a href="#cite_note-edge136-6">[6]</a></sup> Eventually he shifted his focus to making films with his friend who had an <a href="/wiki/8_mm_video_format" title="8 mm video format">8mm</a> camera.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-edge136_6-7"><a href="#cite_note-edge136-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Career">Career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hideo_Kojima&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In an interview on <a href="/wiki/G4_(U.S._TV_channel)" title="G4 (U.S. TV channel)">G4</a>'s TV series <i>Icons</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-G4TV_Icons_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-G4TV_Icons-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> Kojima describes much of his earlier career and influences for game design. Kojima grew up early in life watching movies with his parents. While studying economics in university, Kojima found himself playing video games during his free time, mainly games on the <a href="/wiki/Nintendo_Entertainment_System" title="Nintendo Entertainment System">Famicom</a>. In his fourth year in university, Kojima surprised his peers by announcing his intentions to join the video game industry, despite initially having ambitions of becoming a <a href="/wiki/Film_director" title="Film director">film director</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gamespy_interview_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-gamespy_interview-11">[11]</a></sup> He felt a career in video games would be more satisfying.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RG-35_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-RG-35-12">[12]</a></sup> The majority of his friends and peers strongly discouraged Kojima from pursuing video games due to it being a new medium that wasn't as respected or financially secure. His mother, however, remained supportive which gave Kojima the confidence to go ahead with his dream. He would later reflect positively upon his choice, stating, "The industry was full of dropouts, people who felt like games offered them another chance. I met many people in that same situation; we bonded together through that in some sense."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Parkin_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-Parkin-7">[7]</a></sup> Kojima has cited <a href="/wiki/Shigeru_Miyamoto" title="Shigeru Miyamoto">Shigeru Miyamoto</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Super_Mario_Bros." title="Super Mario Bros.">Super Mario Bros.</a></i> (1985)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-businessweek_may09_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-businessweek_may09-8">[8]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Yuji_Horii" title="Yuji Horii">Yuji Horii</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Portopia_Serial_Murder_Case" title="The Portopia Serial Murder Case">The Portopia Serial Murder Case</a></i> (1983)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gspot_storytellers_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-gspot_storytellers-13">[13]</a></sup> as the games that inspired him to make this decision. He also cited <i><a href="/wiki/Hydlide" title="Hydlide">Hydlide</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s <a href="/wiki/Open_world" title="Open world">open world</a> game design as an influence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kojima_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-kojima-14">[14]</a></sup> His literary influences include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kobo_Abe" title="Kobo Abe">Kobo Abe</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ryu_Murakami" title="Ryu Murakami">Ryu Murakami</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yukio_Mishima" title="Yukio Mishima">Yukio Mishima</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kazuaki_Takano" title="Kazuaki Takano">Kazuaki Takano</a>, <a href="/wiki/Project_Itoh" title="Project Itoh">Project Itoh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yasutaka_Tsutsui" title="Yasutaka Tsutsui">Yasutaka Tsutsui</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seicho_Matsumoto" title="Seicho Matsumoto">Seicho Matsumoto</a>, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Levinson" title="Richard Levinson">Richard Levinson</a>, <a href="/wiki/William_Link" title="William Link">William Link</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Paul_Auster" title="Paul Auster">Paul Auster</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1980s">1980s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hideo_Kojima&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1980s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Kojima attempted joining the game business but was unable to do so at first. His game design ideas were rejected but he never gave up and eventually he was accepted. He joined <a href="/wiki/Video_game_publisher" title="Video game publisher">video game publisher</a> <a href="/wiki/Konami" title="Konami">Konami</a>'s <a href="/wiki/MSX" title="MSX">MSX</a> home computer division in 1986 as a designer and 'planner'.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-G4TV_Icons_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-G4TV_Icons-9">[9]</a></sup> Initially, he was disappointed with his assignment, and desired to work on Nintendo Entertainment System and arcade games instead—Kojima felt the color palette of the system was too restrictive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RG-35_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-RG-35-12">[12]</a></sup> Kojima's gameplay ideas were often overlooked initially, and due to his lack of familiarity with programming was repeatedly snubbed for his failures in his initial years at Konami. At one point Kojima considered leaving the company, but he hung on.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-G4TV_Icons_9-2"><a href="#cite_note-G4TV_Icons-9">[9]</a></sup> The first game he worked on was <i><a href="/wiki/Penguin_Adventure" title="Penguin Adventure">Penguin Adventure</a></i>, the sequel to <i><a href="/wiki/Antarctic_Adventure" title="Antarctic Adventure">Antarctic Adventure</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-edge136_6-8"><a href="#cite_note-edge136-6">[6]</a></sup> as an assistant director. It significantly expanded upon the gameplay of <i>Antarctic Adventure</i>, adding more <a href="/wiki/Action_game" title="Action game">action game</a> elements, a greater variety of levels, <a href="/wiki/Role-playing_video_game" title="Role-playing video game">RPG</a> elements such as upgrading equipment,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multiple_endings" title="Multiple endings">multiple endings</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> The first game he actually developed was <i>Lost Warld</i>, an MSX <a href="/wiki/Platform_game" title="Platform game">platform game</a> in <a href="/wiki/1986_in_video_gaming" title="1986 in video gaming">1986</a>. However, the game was ultimately rejected by Kojima's superiors at Konami.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-G4TV_Icons_9-3"><a href="#cite_note-G4TV_Icons-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>Kojima was asked to take over a project, <i><a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_(video_game)" title="Metal Gear (video game)">Metal Gear</a></i>, from a senior associate. Hardware limitations hindered development of the game's combat. Inspired by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Great_Escape_(book)" title="The Great Escape (book)">The Great Escape</a></i>, Kojima altered the gameplay to focus on a prisoner escaping.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RG-35_12-2"><a href="#cite_note-RG-35-12">[12]</a></sup> It was released in <a href="/wiki/1987_in_video_gaming" title="1987 in video gaming">1987</a> for the <a href="/wiki/MSX" title="MSX">MSX</a>2 home computer in Japan and parts of Europe. The game revolves around a special forces operative codenamed <a href="/wiki/Solid_Snake" title="Solid Snake">Solid Snake</a>, who is sent to the fortified state of "Outer Heaven" to stop a nuclear equipped walking tank known as "<a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_(weapon)" title="Metal Gear (weapon)">Metal Gear</a>". <i>Metal Gear</i> is one of the earliest examples of the <a href="/wiki/Stealth_game" title="Stealth game">stealth action game</a> genre, where avoiding encounters from the enemies is emphasized over direct combat. A port of <i>Metal Gear</i> was also released for the <a href="/wiki/Nintendo_Entertainment_System" title="Nintendo Entertainment System">Nintendo Entertainment System</a>. Kojima was not directly involved in the production of this version and he has openly criticized some of the changes made in this version.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gamerstoday_interview_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-gamerstoday_interview-18">[18]</a></sup> Some of these flaws include bad translation, no ending boss fight with "<a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_(video_game)" title="Metal Gear (video game)">Metal Gear</a>" (which was included in the <a href="/wiki/MSX" title="MSX">MSX</a>2 version), and plenty more. Most of these flaws were fixed in the <a href="/wiki/MSX" title="MSX">MSX</a>2 English port included in <i>Metal Gear Solid 3: Subsistence</i> for the <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_2" title="PlayStation 2">PS2</a>, and <i>Metal Gear Solid: HD Collection</i> for the <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_3" title="PlayStation 3">PS3</a> and <a href="/wiki/Xbox_360" title="Xbox 360">360</a>.</p>
<p>His next project was the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Graphic_adventure_game" title="Graphic adventure game">graphic adventure game</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Snatcher_(video_game)" title="Snatcher (video game)">Snatcher</a></i>, released for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NEC_PC-8801" title="NEC PC-8801">NEC PC-8801</a> and MSX2 computer platforms in Japan in <a href="/wiki/1988_in_video_gaming" title="1988 in video gaming">1988</a>. The game, influenced by <a href="/wiki/Science_fiction" title="Science fiction">science fiction</a> works such as <i><a href="/wiki/Blade_Runner" title="Blade Runner">Blade Runner</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Terminator" title="The Terminator">The Terminator</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Bubblegum_Crisis" title="Bubblegum Crisis">Bubblegum Crisis</a></i>, is set in a <a href="/wiki/Apocalyptic_and_post-apocalyptic_fiction" title="Apocalyptic and post-apocalyptic fiction">post-apocalyptic</a> world and centers around an <a href="/wiki/Amnesia" title="Amnesia">amnesiac</a> detective who faces a race of <a href="/wiki/Cyborg" title="Cyborg">cyborgs</a> (the titular Snatchers) that kill their victims, copy their likeness and assume their place in society.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kalata-Snatcher_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kalata-Snatcher-19">[19]</a></sup> While Kojima and his team wrote the entire story of the game, they were forced to leave out the final act of the game due to time constraints. The game was highly regarded at the time for pushing the boundaries of video game storytelling, cinematic <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cut_scene" title="Cut scene">cut scenes</a>, and mature content,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1UP-Kojima_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-1UP-Kojima-20">[20]</a></sup> and was praised for its graphics, soundtrack, high quality writing comparable to a <a href="/wiki/Novel" title="Novel">novel</a>, voice acting comparable to a <a href="/wiki/Film" title="Film">film</a> or <a href="/wiki/Radio_drama" title="Radio drama">radio drama</a>, <a href="/wiki/Apocalyptic_and_post-apocalyptic_fiction" title="Apocalyptic and post-apocalyptic fiction">post-apocalyptic</a> setting, <a href="/wiki/Light_gun_shooter" title="Light gun shooter">light gun shooter</a> segments, and in-game computer database with optional documents that flesh out the game world. The <a href="/wiki/Sega_CD" title="Sega CD">Sega CD</a> version of <i>Snatcher</i> was for a long time the only major visual novel game to be released in America. However, partly due to a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ESRB" title="ESRB">Teen</a> rating limiting its accessibility,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kalata-Snatcher_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kalata-Snatcher-19">[19]</a></sup> it only sold a "couple of thousand units", according to <a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Blaustein" title="Jeremy Blaustein">Jeremy Blaustein</a>, a member of <i>Snatcher'</i>s localization team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Blaustein_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-Blaustein-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1990s">1990s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hideo_Kojima&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 1990s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/1990_in_video_gaming" title="1990 in video gaming">1990</a>, Kojima was involved in the productions of two MSX2 games: a spinoff of <i>Snatcher</i> titled <i><a href="/wiki/SD_Snatcher" title="SD Snatcher">SD Snatcher</a></i>; and a sequel to <i>Metal Gear</i> titled <i><a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_2:_Solid_Snake" title="Metal Gear 2: Solid Snake">Metal Gear 2: Solid Snake</a></i>, which further evolved the <a href="/wiki/Stealth_game" title="Stealth game">stealth game</a> genre. The player had more abilities, such as crouching, crawling into hiding spots and air ducts, distracting guards by knocking on surfaces, and using a radar to plan ahead. The enemies had improved <a href="/wiki/Artificial_intelligence" title="Artificial intelligence">AI</a>, including a 45-degree field of vision, the detection of various different noises, being able to move from screen to screen, and a three-phase security alarm. The game also had improved graphics and a complex storyline dealing with themes such as the nature of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Warfare" title="Warfare">warfare</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_disarmament" title="Nuclear disarmament">nuclear disarmament</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GameSpy_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-GameSpy-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>SD Snatcher</i> is a <a href="/wiki/Role-playing_video_game" title="Role-playing video game">role-playing video game</a> which adapts the storyline of the original <i>Snatcher</i>, while featuring its version of the planned ending. The characters are depicted in a "<a href="/wiki/Super_deformed" title="Super deformed">super deformed</a>" art style, in contrast to the original game's realistic style. Like the original computer versions of <i>Snatcher</i>, it was only released in Japan. It abandoned <a href="/wiki/Random_encounter" title="Random encounter">random encounters</a> and introduced an innovative <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_person_(video_games)" title="First person (video games)">first-person</a> turn-based battle system where the player can aim at specific parts of the enemy's body using firearms with limited ammo. Such a battle system has rarely been used since,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kalata-Snatcher_19-2"><a href="#cite_note-Kalata-Snatcher-19">[19]</a></sup> though similar battle systems based on targeting individual body parts can later be found in <a href="/wiki/Square_(company)" title="Square (company)">Square</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Vagrant_Story" title="Vagrant Story">Vagrant Story</a></i> (2000), <a href="/wiki/Bethesda_Softworks" title="Bethesda Softworks">Bethesda</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Fallout_3" title="Fallout 3">Fallout 3</a></i> (2008), and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nippon_Ichi" title="Nippon Ichi">Nippon Ichi</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Last_Rebellion" title="Last Rebellion">Last Rebellion</a></i> (2010).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>Due to the success of the original <i>Metal Gear</i> on the NES, Konami decided to create a sequel to the game, <i><a href="/wiki/Snake%27s_Revenge" title="Snake's Revenge">Snake's Revenge</a></i>, without the involvement of Kojima. During a ride home on the train, Kojima met one of the staff members who worked on the game who asked him if he would create a "true" <i>Metal Gear</i> sequel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-G4TV_Icons_9-4"><a href="#cite_note-G4TV_Icons-9">[9]</a></sup> As a result, Kojima began plans for his own sequel titled: <i>Metal Gear 2: Solid Snake</i>. The game was only released in Japan for the MSX2, as one of the last games Konami produced for the computer system. The game would not be released overseas in North America and Europe until its inclusion in <a href="/wiki/2006_in_video_gaming" title="2006 in video gaming">2006</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_Solid_3:_Snake_Eater#Subsistence" title="Metal Gear Solid 3: Snake Eater">Metal Gear Solid 3: Subsistence</a></i>.</p>
<p>All of his subsequent projects after <i>Metal Gear 2</i> were produced primarily for <a href="/wiki/Optical_disc" title="Optical disc">disc</a>-based media, allowing for the inclusion of voice acting in his games. He remade <i>Snatcher</i> in <a href="/wiki/1992_in_video_gaming" title="1992 in video gaming">1992</a> for the <a href="/wiki/TurboGrafx-16" title="TurboGrafx-16">PC Engine Super CD-ROM<sup>2</sup></a>. An English localization of the game was produced for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sega_Mega-CD" title="Sega Mega-CD">Sega Mega-CD</a> in North America and Europe in <a href="/wiki/1994_in_video_gaming" title="1994 in video gaming">1994</a>. Kojima was not directly involved in the Sega CD version nor the subsequent PlayStation and Saturn ports released in <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a> in <a href="/wiki/1996_in_video_gaming" title="1996 in video gaming">1996</a>.</p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/1994_in_video_gaming" title="1994 in video gaming">1994</a>, Kojima released <i><a href="/wiki/Policenauts" title="Policenauts">Policenauts</a></i>, a <a href="/wiki/Film_noir" title="Film noir">film noir</a>/<a href="/wiki/Science_fiction" title="Science fiction">sci-fi</a>-themed <a href="/wiki/Adventure_game" title="Adventure game">adventure game</a> set in a space colony, for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PC-9801" title="PC-9801">NEC PC-9821</a>. Kojima oversaw the subsequent ports released for the <a href="/wiki/3DO_Interactive_Multiplayer" title="3DO Interactive Multiplayer">3DO</a> in <a href="/wiki/1995_in_video_gaming" title="1995 in video gaming">1995</a>; and the PlayStation and Saturn in <a href="/wiki/1996_in_video_gaming" title="1996 in video gaming">1996</a>, which all featured animated cut-scenes not in the PC-98 release. Despite announcements for an English release in 1996,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> problems with synching the English dialogue with the cut-scenes stopped its production.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kojimaoshii_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-kojimaoshii-26">[26]</a></sup> An unofficial English translation patch was released to the public at midnight (<a href="/wiki/Japan_Standard_Time" title="Japan Standard Time">JST</a>) on August 24, 2009, to coincide with Kojima's 46th birthday.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> From 1997 to 1999, he developed the <i><a href="/wiki/Tokimeki_Memorial_(series)" title="Tokimeki Memorial (series)">Tokimeki Memorial Drama Series</a></i>, a trilogy of <a href="/wiki/Visual_novel" title="Visual novel">visual novel</a> adventure games.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>With the release of <i><a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_Solid" title="Metal Gear Solid">Metal Gear Solid</a></i> (<i>MGS</i>) in <a href="/wiki/1998_in_video_gaming" title="1998 in video gaming">1998</a> for the <a href="/wiki/PlayStation" title="PlayStation">PlayStation</a>, Kojima became an international <a href="/wiki/Celebrity" title="Celebrity">celebrity</a> among the video game media. <i>Metal Gear Solid</i> was the first in the <i>Metal Gear</i> series to use 3D graphics and voice acting, which gave a more cinematic experience to the game. <i>MGS</i> was highly regarded for its well-designed gameplay and for its characters and storyline, which featured themes of <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_proliferation" title="Nuclear proliferation">nuclear proliferation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Genetic_engineering" title="Genetic engineering">genetic engineering</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2000s">2000s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hideo_Kojima&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2000s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In early 2001, Kojima released the first details of the <a href="/wiki/Sequel" title="Sequel">sequel</a> to <i>Metal Gear Solid</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_Solid_2:_Sons_of_Liberty" title="Metal Gear Solid 2: Sons of Liberty">Metal Gear Solid 2: Sons of Liberty</a></i>, for the <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_2" title="PlayStation 2">PlayStation 2</a>. The game's highly detailed <a href="/wiki/Computer_graphics" title="Computer graphics">graphics</a>, physics, and expanded gameplay quickly made it one of the most anticipated games yet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> The game was highly successful and critically acclaimed at release, due to its graphics, gameplay and storyline, which dealt with myriad philosophical themes as specific as <a href="/wiki/Meme" title="Meme">memes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Censorship" title="Censorship">censorship</a>, manipulation, patricide, the inherent flaws of <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">democracy</a> and as grandiose as the nature of reality itself. While <i>Metal Gear Solid 2</i> appealed to gamers with the discussion of these, the bewildering maze of dialogue and plot revelation in the final hours of the game left a sour taste in the mouths of many gamers, who expected the Hollywood-style resolution of its forerunner.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>Before the release of <i>MGS2</i>, Kojima produced the game and <a href="/wiki/Anime" title="Anime">anime</a> franchise <i><a href="/wiki/Zone_of_the_Enders" title="Zone of the Enders">Zone of the Enders</a></i> in 2001 to moderate success. In 2003, he produced <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Boktai:_The_Sun_Is_in_Your_Hand" title="Boktai: The Sun Is in Your Hand">Boktai: The Sun Is in Your Hand</a></i> for the <a href="/wiki/Game_Boy_Advance" title="Game Boy Advance">Game Boy Advance</a>, which players take the role of a young vampire hunter who uses a solar weapon which is charged by a <a href="/wiki/Photometry_(optics)" title="Photometry (optics)">photometric</a> sensor on the game cartridge (forcing them to play in sunlight). Another team inside Konami (in a collaboration with <a href="/wiki/Silicon_Knights" title="Silicon Knights">Silicon Knights</a>) began work on <i><a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_Solid:_The_Twin_Snakes" title="Metal Gear Solid: The Twin Snakes">Metal Gear Solid: The Twin Snakes</a></i>, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nintendo_GameCube" title="Nintendo GameCube">GameCube</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Enhanced_remake" title="Enhanced remake">remake</a> of the first <i>Metal Gear Solid</i> with all the gameplay features of <i>Metal Gear Solid 2</i> and with cutscenes redirected by <a href="/wiki/Action_film" title="Action film">action</a>/<a href="/wiki/Horror_film" title="Horror film">horror film</a> director <a href="/wiki/Ryuhei_Kitamura" title="Ryuhei Kitamura">Ryuhei Kitamura</a>. It was released in 2004.</p>
<p>Afterwards, Kojima also designed and released <i><a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_Solid_3:_Snake_Eater" title="Metal Gear Solid 3: Snake Eater">Metal Gear Solid 3: Snake Eater</a></i> for the PlayStation 2. Unlike the previous games in the series, which took place in the near future and focused on indoor locations, the game is set in a Soviet jungle during the height of the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> in 1964, and features wilderness survival, camouflage, and <i><a href="/wiki/James_Bond" title="James Bond">James Bond</a></i> styled espionage. The North American version was released on November 17, 2004, with the Japanese counterpart following on December 16. The European version was released on March 4, 2005. Critical response to the game was highly favorable. Kojima has said that his mother even played it, "It took her an entire year to complete Metal Gear Solid 3. She would get her friends to help her. When she defeated The End, [a character the player faces off during the game] she called me up and said: 'It is finished'."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>At that time Kojima produced <i>Boktai'</i>s sequel, <i><a href="/wiki/Boktai_2:_Solar_Boy_Django" title="Boktai 2: Solar Boy Django">Boktai 2: Solar Boy Django</a></i> for the <a href="/wiki/Game_Boy_Advance" title="Game Boy Advance">Game Boy Advance</a>. Released in summer 2004, it makes more extensive use of the cartridge's sunlight sensor and allows players to combine various new solar weapons. Also released was <i><a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_Acid" title="Metal Gear Acid">Metal Gear Acid</a></i> for the <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_Portable" title="PlayStation Portable">PlayStation Portable</a> handheld. This <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Turn-based_game" title="Turn-based game">turn-based game</a> is less action-oriented than the other <i>Metal Gear</i> games and focuses more on <a href="/wiki/Strategy" title="Strategy">strategy</a>. It was released in Japan on December 16, 2004. Its sequel <i><a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_Acid_2" title="Metal Gear Acid 2">Metal Gear Acid 2</a></i> was released on March 21, 2006.</p>
<p>Kojima wanted Solid Snake to appear in Nintendo's <i><a href="/wiki/Super_Smash_Bros._Melee" title="Super Smash Bros. Melee">Super Smash Bros. Melee</a></i>, but Nintendo refused, due to development cycle problems. When <i><a href="/wiki/Super_Smash_Bros._Brawl" title="Super Smash Bros. Brawl">Super Smash Bros. Brawl</a></i> was in development, series director <a href="/wiki/Masahiro_Sakurai" title="Masahiro Sakurai">Masahiro Sakurai</a> contacted Kojima to work and add Snake and his stage into the game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>Released in June 2008, Kojima co-directed <i><a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_Solid_4:_Guns_of_the_Patriots" title="Metal Gear Solid 4: Guns of the Patriots">Metal Gear Solid 4: Guns of the Patriots</a></i> with Shuyo Murata. Initially, Kojima was not going to direct it, but death threats made the team nervous and he decided to work with them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> Kojima received a lifetime achievement award at the MTV Game Awards 2008 in Germany. In his speech, he said in English, "I have to say, even though I received this award, let me state that I will not retire. I will continue to create games as long as I live."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-joystiq_ltaa_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-joystiq_ltaa-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>Before E3 2009, Kojima stated interest in working with a western developer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> This later turned out to be a collaboration between him and <a href="/wiki/MercurySteam" title="MercurySteam">MercurySteam</a> to work on <i><a href="/wiki/Castlevania:_Lords_of_Shadow" title="Castlevania: Lords of Shadow">Castlevania: Lords of Shadow</a></i>.</p>
<p>Although he announced that <i>Metal Gear Solid 4: Guns of the Patriots</i> would be the last <i>Metal Gear</i> game he would be directly involved in,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kikizo_aug2008_2_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-kikizo_aug2008_2-37">[37]</a></sup> he announced at E3 2009 that he would return to help on two <i>Metal Gear</i> games: <i><a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_Rising:_Revengeance" title="Metal Gear Rising: Revengeance">Metal Gear Solid: Rising</a></i>, as a producer and <i><a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_Solid:_Peace_Walker" title="Metal Gear Solid: Peace Walker">Metal Gear Solid: Peace Walker</a></i> as writer, director and producer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> When interviewed at <a href="/wiki/Gamescom" title="Gamescom">Gamescom 2009</a>, Kojima stated that he got more involved with <i>Peace Walker</i> because, "there was a lot of confusion within the team and it didn't proceed as I wanted it to. Therefore I thought that I needed to jump in and do <i>Peace Walker</i>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gamescon2009_ign_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-gamescon2009_ign-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2010s">2010s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hideo_Kojima&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2010s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hideo_Kojima_-_PlayStation.Blog_E3_Meetup_-_2010.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2384" data-file-width="3583" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Hideo_Kojima_-_PlayStation.Blog_E3_Meetup_-_2010.jpg/220px-Hideo_Kojima_-_PlayStation.Blog_E3_Meetup_-_2010.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Hideo_Kojima_-_PlayStation.Blog_E3_Meetup_-_2010.jpg/330px-Hideo_Kojima_-_PlayStation.Blog_E3_Meetup_-_2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Hideo_Kojima_-_PlayStation.Blog_E3_Meetup_-_2010.jpg/440px-Hideo_Kojima_-_PlayStation.Blog_E3_Meetup_-_2010.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hideo_Kojima_-_PlayStation.Blog_E3_Meetup_-_2010.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Kojima (right) with translator Aki Saito in 2010</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Kojima was at E3 2010 to show off his team's latest project, <i><a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_Rising:_Revengeance" title="Metal Gear Rising: Revengeance">Metal Gear: Rising</a></i>, but a report from CVG says the game developer has a "massive PS3 exclusive" to unveil at <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Game_Show" title="Tokyo Game Show">Tokyo Game Show</a> however nothing to date has been mentioned.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> He was also seen in Nintendo's 3DS interview video, where he stated he was interested in making a <i>Metal Gear Solid</i> game for the 3DS and wondered what it would be like in 3D.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> This game ended up being a remake of <i>Metal Gear Solid 3</i> titled <i><a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_Solid_3:_Snake_Eater#Metal_Gear_Solid:_Snake_Eater_3D" title="Metal Gear Solid 3: Snake Eater">Metal Gear Solid: Snake Eater 3D</a></i>. In late 2011, <i>Metal Gear Solid: Rising</i> was renamed <i>Metal Gear Rising: Revengeance</i> with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Platinum_Games" title="Platinum Games">Platinum Games</a> being involved in developing it alongside Kojima Productions. Nevertheless, Kojima is the game's executive producer and showed interest in working in the game's demo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> Kojima was satisfied with the final product and expressed the possibility of a sequel if Platinum were to develop it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>On April 1, 2011, Kojima was promoted to be the Vice President of Konami Digital Entertainment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> At <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/E3_2011" title="E3 2011">E3 2011</a>, he revealed his new innovative gaming technology labeled as "transfarring", a <i><a href="/wiki/Portmanteau" title="Portmanteau">portmanteau</a></i> of the verbs <i>transferring</i> and <i>sharing</i>. This new technology enables gamers to transfer their gaming data from the PS3 to PSP in a quick data transferring process and bring it on the go from home into the outside world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p>Later that year, he stated he was working on a new <a href="/wiki/Intellectual_property" title="Intellectual property">intellectual property</a> with <a href="/wiki/Goichi_Suda" title="Goichi Suda">Suda-51</a>, tentatively titled <i>Project S</i>, and preparing new projects. On July 8, 2011, Kojima announced that <i>Project S</i> was a radio-show sequel to <i><a href="/wiki/Snatcher_(video_game)" title="Snatcher (video game)">Snatcher</a></i>, titled <i>Sdatcher</i> as a reference to the show's producer Suda-51. The show would air on Fridays on Kojima's bi-weekly Internet radio show, starting with episode #300 which was broadcast in August 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> In October, Kojima announced that he would be collaborating with Suda51 and <a href="/wiki/5pb." title="5pb.">5pb.</a> director Chiyomaru Shikura in producing a new <a href="/wiki/Adventure_game" title="Adventure game">adventure game</a> <a href="/wiki/Visual_novel" title="Visual novel">visual novel</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> It was initially speculated that the game would be the <a href="/wiki/Robotics;Notes" title="Robotics;Notes">third entry</a> in 5pb.'s Science Adventure series, but was later confirmed to be a separate title.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> The game was planned to have an overseas release and an anime adaption.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> As of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hideo_Kojima&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, no new info has surfaced of the proposed project.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In mid-2012 and in the following years after Kojima finished work on the <a href="/wiki/Fox_Engine" title="Fox Engine">Fox Engine</a>, Kojima has been unofficially connected to the <i><a href="/wiki/Silent_Hill" title="Silent Hill">Silent Hill</a></i> series. During this time, he indicated that he was interested in making a Silent Hill game and the first instance of this was on 18 August 2012. He described his excitement regarding the potential use of the Fox Engine on the 8th generation platforms via a tweet of an image of the DVD for the Silent Hill movie:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> Later, he added what he had in mind for this game in a series of tweets: "Silent Hill is in closed room setting and doesn’t require full action so that we can focus on the graphic quality. Enemies featured in the game do not have to be consistent or move fast. It only requires scariness by graphics and presentation. As being a creator, making action games in an open world setting, such a type of game is very enviously attractive. If only someone could create this on the FOX engine."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> After a while, and as a result of Kojima’s interest in making a Silent Hill game, Konami officially asked him to do so. Kojima then explained the story in an interview with Eurogamer:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>In the past I’ve mentioned Silent Hill in interviews, and as a result of that the president of Konami rung me up and said he’d like me to make the next Silent Hill. Honestly, I’m kind of a scaredy-cat when it comes to horror movies, so I’m not confident I can do it. At the same time, there’s a certain type of horror that only people who are scared of can create, so maybe it’s something I can do. That said, I think Silent Hill has a certain atmosphere. I think it has to continue, and I’d love to help it continue, and if I can help by supervising or lending the technology of the Fox Engine, then I’d love to participate in that respect.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>Additionally, in an interview with Canadian gaming journalist, <a href="/wiki/Geoff_Keighley" title="Geoff Keighley">Geoff Keighley</a>, when a fan asked “which game do you want to direct or reboot?” Kojima stated without hesitation, "Silent Hill".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> Keighley jumped in and asked "What do you want to do with Silent Hill?" Kojima responded: "A guy [like myself] that is such a chicken and is so easily scared – making a scary game – I’m very confident that something horrifying would come out from that. But on the other hand I would have to prepare myself to have nightmares every single day. Hopefully sometime in the future I’m able to work on this, but I would really need to prepare to have daily nightmares."<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In August 2014, a <a href="/wiki/P.T._(video_game)" title="P.T. (video game)">playable teaser</a> trailer released on the <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_Store" title="PlayStation Store">PlayStation Store</a> revealed that a new game in the <i><a href="/wiki/Silent_Hill" title="Silent Hill">Silent Hill</a></i> franchise titled <i><a href="/wiki/Silent_Hills" title="Silent Hills">Silent Hills</a></i> was being directed by Kojima for the <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_4" title="PlayStation 4">PlayStation 4</a>, alongside Mexican film director <a href="/wiki/Guillermo_del_Toro" title="Guillermo del Toro">Guillermo del Toro</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> In April 2015, the playable trailer was removed and the game was officially cancelled.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the 2013 <a href="/wiki/Game_Developers_Conference" title="Game Developers Conference">Game Developers Conference</a>, Kojima unveiled <i><a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_Solid_V:_The_Phantom_Pain" title="Metal Gear Solid V: The Phantom Pain">Metal Gear Solid V: The Phantom Pain</a></i>, which is set to be his final <i>Metal Gear</i> work, noting that this time unlike previous announcements that he had stopped working on the series, was very serious about leaving.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> In March 2015, reports began to surface that Kojima would part ways with longtime publisher Konami after the release of <i>The Phantom Pain</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> Konami later stated that they were auditioning for new staff for future <i>Metal Gear</i> titles and removed Kojima's name from the series's marketing material.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> Despite reports that Kojima left the company in October 2015, a spokesman for Konami stated that he was "taking a long time off from work."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> At <a href="/wiki/The_Game_Awards_2015" title="The Game Awards 2015">The Game Awards 2015</a>, <i>Metal Gear Solid V</i> won the awards for Best Action Game and Best Score/Soundtrack, but Kojima did not attend the event, being reportedly barred from attending by Konami.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Konamiban_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-Konamiban-63">[63]</a></sup> Instead, it was accepted by <a href="/wiki/Kiefer_Sutherland" title="Kiefer Sutherland">Kiefer Sutherland</a> on his behalf.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Konamiban_63-1"><a href="#cite_note-Konamiban-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<p>On December 16, 2015, Kojima released a joint statement with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sony_Computer_Entertainment" title="Sony Computer Entertainment">Sony Computer Entertainment</a>, announcing that Kojima Productions would be re-established as an independent studio and that their first game would be console exclusive to the <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_4" title="PlayStation 4">PlayStation 4</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-polygon-kojimasony_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-polygon-kojimasony-64">[64]</a></sup> At <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/E3_2016" title="E3 2016">E3 2016</a> in Los Angeles, Kojima personally showed up to announce the game's title, which was revealed as <i><a href="/wiki/Death_Stranding" title="Death Stranding">Death Stranding</a></i> in a trailer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> The trailer also showed actor and inspiration for the main character <a href="/wiki/Norman_Reedus" title="Norman Reedus">Norman Reedus</a>, who Kojima had previously worked with in the canceled <i>Silent Hills</i>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Works">Works</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hideo_Kojima&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Works">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Metal_Gear_series"><i>Metal Gear</i> series</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hideo_Kojima&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Metal Gear series">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Influences_and_mentality">Influences and mentality</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hideo_Kojima&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Influences and mentality">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Kojima has cited <a href="/wiki/Yuji_Horii" title="Yuji Horii">Yuji Horii</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Portopia_Serial_Murder_Case" title="The Portopia Serial Murder Case">The Portopia Serial Murder Case</a></i> (1983)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gspot_storytellers_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-gspot_storytellers-13">[13]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Shigeru_Miyamoto" title="Shigeru Miyamoto">Shigeru Miyamoto</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Super_Mario_Bros." title="Super Mario Bros.">Super Mario Bros.</a></i> (1985)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-businessweek_may09_8-2"><a href="#cite_note-businessweek_may09-8">[8]</a></sup> as the games that inspired him to enter the <a href="/wiki/Video_game_industry" title="Video game industry">video game industry</a>. <i>Portopia Serial Murder Case</i>, a <a href="/wiki/Crime_fiction" title="Crime fiction">murder mystery</a> adventure game, was an important influence because, according to Kojima, it had "mystery, a 3D dungeon, humor, and a proper background and explanation of why the murderer committed the crime. That is why there was drama in this game. My encountering this game expanded the potential of video games in my mind."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gspot_storytellers_13-2"><a href="#cite_note-gspot_storytellers-13">[13]</a></sup> <i>Portopia</i> had an influence on his early works, including <i>Metal Gear</i> and particularly <i>Snatcher</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Retro-85_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-Retro-85-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<p>Kojima's love of <a href="/wiki/Film" title="Film">film</a> is noticeable in his games where he pays <a href="/wiki/Homage_(arts)" title="Homage (arts)">homage</a> through his stories and characters, sometimes to the point of <a href="/wiki/Pastiche" title="Pastiche">pastiche</a>, as in <i><a href="/wiki/Snatcher_(video_game)" title="Snatcher (video game)">Snatcher</a></i>. He cited a contrast between films and games as while in his games he intends to portray violence like in a movie, in the game it is up to the player to decide. He wants people to understand the effects of violence. As he considers the games too stressful, he also wants comic relief to contrast it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>Snatcher</i> is inspired by many science fiction movies, particularly from the eighties, including <i><a href="/wiki/Blade_Runner" title="Blade Runner">Blade Runner</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Akira_(1988_film)" title="Akira (1988 film)">Akira</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gamecritics_snatcher_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-gamecritics_snatcher-69">[69]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Thing_(1982_film)" title="The Thing (1982 film)">The Thing</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_the_Body_Snatchers" title="Invasion of the Body Snatchers">Invasion of the Body Snatchers</a></i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Terminator" title="The Terminator">The Terminator</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gamecritics_snatcher_69-1"><a href="#cite_note-gamecritics_snatcher-69">[69]</a></sup> Examples of influence by films include Solid Snake's codename (named after <a href="/wiki/Snake_Plissken" title="Snake Plissken">Snake Plissken</a> from <i><a href="/wiki/Escape_from_New_York" title="Escape from New York">Escape from New York</a></i>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gamerstoday_interview_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-gamerstoday_interview-18">[18]</a></sup> Snake's alias in <i>MGS2</i>: Pliskin (in reference to the last name of Snake Plissken from the <i>Escape</i> movies), Snake's real name (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/David_Bowman_(Space_Odyssey)" title="David Bowman (Space Odyssey)">Dave</a> from <i><a href="/wiki/2001:_A_Space_Odyssey_(film)" title="2001: A Space Odyssey (film)">2001: A Space Odyssey</a></i>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-making_of_mgs2_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-making_of_mgs2-71">[71]</a></sup> and Snake's trademark bandana (<i><a href="/wiki/The_Deer_Hunter" title="The Deer Hunter">The Deer Hunter</a></i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup>).</p>
<p>Movies would also have influence on other aspects of his games. Hal "Otacon" Emmerich (named after <a href="/wiki/HAL_9000" title="HAL 9000">HAL</a> from <i>2001: A Space Odyssey</i> and film director <a href="/wiki/Roland_Emmerich" title="Roland Emmerich">Roland Emmerich</a>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-making_of_mgs2_71-1"><a href="#cite_note-making_of_mgs2-71">[71]</a></sup> Sniper Wolf shooting Meryl in <i>Metal Gear Solid</i> (<i><a href="/wiki/Full_Metal_Jacket" title="Full Metal Jacket">Full Metal Jacket</a></i>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gamerstoday_interview_18-2"><a href="#cite_note-gamerstoday_interview-18">[18]</a></sup> Psycho Mantis (inspired from the film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Fury_(1978_film)" title="The Fury (1978 film)">The Fury</a></i>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gamerstoday_interview_18-3"><a href="#cite_note-gamerstoday_interview-18">[18]</a></sup> and the whole <i>Metal Gear</i> stealth concept (<i><a href="/wiki/The_Great_Escape_(film)" title="The Great Escape (film)">The Great Escape</a></i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gamerstoday_interview_18-4"><a href="#cite_note-gamerstoday_interview-18">[18]</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guns_of_Navarone_(film)" title="The Guns of Navarone (film)">The Guns of Navarone</a></i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup>). James Bond also had a large influence on the Metal Gear series,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> with <i>Metal Gear Solid 3</i> having a <i>James Bond</i>-like introduction sequence.</p>
<p>In an article he wrote for Official PlayStation 2 Magazine, Hideo described the influence of the film <i><a href="/wiki/Dawn_of_the_Dead_(1978_film)" title="Dawn of the Dead (1978 film)">Dawn of the Dead</a></i> on the Metal Gear series. The zombie classic inspired "the maximum three-dimensional use of a closed area like a shopping mall with elevators, air ducts, and escalators." These aspects are similar enough in his view that "MGS is DOTD if you replace soldiers with zombies."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<p>He also received inspiration from <a href="/wiki/Anime" title="Anime">anime</a>. His early works, particularly the <a href="/wiki/Cyberpunk" title="Cyberpunk">cyberpunk</a> adventure game <i>Snatcher</i> (which uses anime-style art), were influenced by cyberpunk anime, most notably <i>Akira</i> (mentioned above).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gamecritics_snatcher_69-2"><a href="#cite_note-gamecritics_snatcher-69">[69]</a></sup> In a recent interview, he mentioned that his <i>Zone of the Enders</i> series was inspired by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mecha_anime" title="Mecha anime">mecha/robot anime</a>, such as <i><a href="/wiki/Neon_Genesis_Evangelion" title="Neon Genesis Evangelion">Neon Genesis Evangelion</a></i>. Mecha anime were also an inspiration for the <i>Metal Gear</i> series, which features <a href="/wiki/Mecha" title="Mecha">mecha</a> robots, such as <a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_(weapon)#Metal_Gear_REX" title="Metal Gear (weapon)">Metal Gear REX</a> and <a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_(weapon)#Metal_Gear_RAY" title="Metal Gear (weapon)">Metal Gear RAY</a>; this is referenced in <i>Metal Gear Solid</i>, where Otacon mentions mecha anime as an influence on his Metal Gear REX designs.</p>
<p>In regards to storyline development and interaction with them, he said:</p>
<table class="cquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">
<tr>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">“</td>
<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">Storytelling is very difficult. But adding the flavor helps to relay the storytelling, meaning in a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cut_scene" title="Cut scene">cut scene</a>, with a set camera and effects, you can make the users feel sorrow, or make them happy or laugh. This is an easy approach, which we have been doing. That is one point, the second point is that if I make multiple storylines and allow the users to select which story, this might really sacrifice the deep emotion the user might feel; when there's a concrete storyline, and you kind of go along that rail, you feel the destiny of the story, which at the end, makes you feel more moved. But when you make it interactive — if you want multiple stories where you go one way or another — will that make the player more moved when he or she finishes the game? These two points are really the key which I am thinking about, and if this works, I think I could probably introduce a <a href="/wiki/Nonlinear_gameplay" title="Nonlinear gameplay">more interactive</a> storytelling method.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></td>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">”</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>In terms of reverse influence on film, his work on the storylines of the <i>Metal Gear</i> series was cited as an influence by <a href="/wiki/Screenwriter" title="Screenwriter">screenwriter</a> <a href="/wiki/David_Hayter" title="David Hayter">David Hayter</a>, the voice actor for Solid Snake, on his <a href="/wiki/Screenwriting" title="Screenwriting">screenwriting</a> for <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_the_United_States" title="Cinema of the United States">Hollywood films</a>. He stated that "Kojima and I have different styles," "but I've certainly learned things from him, especially about ambiguity and telling a story without giving all the answers."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HayterSnake_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-HayterSnake-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<p>In an interview Kojima gave to the Metal Gear Solid Official Mission Handbook in 1998, he listed these people as his all-time favorite filmmakers: <a href="/wiki/Stanley_Kubrick" title="Stanley Kubrick">Stanley Kubrick</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luc_Besson" title="Luc Besson">Luc Besson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jean_Cocteau" title="Jean Cocteau">Jean Cocteau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Krzysztof_Kie%C5%9Blowski" title="Krzysztof Kieślowski">Krzysztof Kieślowski</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tony_Scott" title="Tony Scott">Tony Scott</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Lynch" title="David Lynch">David Lynch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Danny_Boyle" title="Danny Boyle">Danny Boyle</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_Cameron" title="James Cameron">James Cameron</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Carpenter" title="John Carpenter">John Carpenter</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jan_Kounen" title="Jan Kounen">Jan Kounen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dario_Argento" title="Dario Argento">Dario Argento</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_A._Romero" title="George A. Romero">George A. Romero</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ridley_Scott" title="Ridley Scott">Ridley Scott</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sam_Raimi" title="Sam Raimi">Sam Raimi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peter_Jackson" title="Peter Jackson">Peter Jackson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quentin_Tarantino" title="Quentin Tarantino">Quentin Tarantino</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Woo" title="John Woo">John Woo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Rodriguez" title="Robert Rodriguez">Robert Rodriguez</a>, <a href="/wiki/Akira_Kurosawa" title="Akira Kurosawa">Akira Kurosawa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Masayuki_Suo" title="Masayuki Suo">Masayuki Suo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/George_Iida" title="George Iida">Joji Iida</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_accolades">Awards and accolades</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hideo_Kojima&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Awards and accolades">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Newsweek" title="Newsweek">Newsweek</a></i> named Hideo Kojima as one of the top ten people of 2002.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> In 2008, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Next_Generation_Magazine" title="Next Generation Magazine">Next-Gen</a></i> placed him seventh in their list of "Hot 100 Developers 2008."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2009, <a href="/wiki/IGN" title="IGN">IGN</a> placed him sixth in their list of top game creators of all time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> At the 2008 MTV Game Awards, Hideo was given the award show's first Lifetime Achievement Award for a game designer and was also honored with a Lifetime Achievement Award at the 2009 <a href="/wiki/Game_Developers_Conference" title="Game Developers Conference">Game Developers Conference</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gdc_2009_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-gdc_2009-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<p>In December 2015, Kojima was invited to accept an award from <a href="/wiki/The_Game_Awards_2015" title="The Game Awards 2015">The Game Awards</a> for Metal Gear Solid: The Phantom Pain. However Konami prevented him from attending the awards ceremony.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<p>In February 2016, he received the AIAS Hall of Fame Award at 19th Annual <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/D.I.C.E._Awards" title="D.I.C.E. Awards">D.I.C.E. Awards</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<p>In December 2016, he was able to attend <a href="/wiki/The_Game_Awards_2016" title="The Game Awards 2016">The Game Awards 2016</a> and accepted their Industry Icon Award.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tga2016_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-tga2016-86">[86]</a></sup></p>

Retrieved <span class="nowrap">2009-08-07</span></span>. <q>メタルギア誕生に最も影響を受けたのは、諜報アクション映画である007シリーズ。ショーン・コネリー演じる初代ボンドの作品の中で最も娯楽性に富んでいるのがこの作品。のちのボンド映画の手本となった。</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AHideo+Kojima&amp;rft.btitle=%E3%8CMGS%E3%82%B7%E3%83%AA%E3%83%BC%E3%82%BA%E3%81%AB%E5%BD%B1%E9%9F%BF%E3%82%92%E4%B8%8E%E3%81%88%E3%81%9F%E5%81%89%E5%A4%A7%E3%81%AA%E3%8215%E3%81%AE%E6%98%A0%E7%94%BB%E4%BD%9C%E5%93%81%E3%E7%89%B9%E9%9B%86+-+3&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.tsutaya.co.jp%2Fmovie%2Fsp%2Fmgs4%2Fcinema03.html&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span> <span class="languageicon" style="font-size:0.95em; font-weight:bold; color:#555;">(Japanese)</span></span></li>
